#### *Galactic Starfighter*

 [![Galactic Starfighter](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/a/a8/Galactic_Starfighter.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20131008205231) [![Galactic Starfighter](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/a/a8/Galactic_Starfighter.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/250?cb=20131008205231)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/a/a8/Galactic_Starfighter.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20131008205231) 

*Galactic Starfighter*

 

:   [![icon](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/04/Blue_Glass_Arrow.svg/revision/latest?cb=20090726033133) Main article: [Star Wars: The Old Republic: Galactic Starfighter](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Old_Republic:_Galactic_Starfighter "Star Wars: The Old Republic: Galactic Starfighter")

:   "*Galactic Starfighter is a 12v12 PvP free flight space shooter. At its core, it is all about coming as close as we can to recreating the incredible experience of space combat as seen in the Star Wars™ movies. It is fast, furious dogfighting action where you get to choose your style of play by selecting the Starfighter that is right for you, be it Scout, Strike Fighter or Gunship (or all of the above!), blowing up your enemies, and then using Requisition (experience) to upgrade and customize your ships.*"
:   ―Blaine Christine[[65]](#cite_note-Welcome_to_Galactic_Starfighter_Early_Access-65)

***Galactic Starfighter*** is the second Digital Expansion for *The Old Republic*, and it was first officially announced on October 8, 2013 with an intended release to the general public in February 2014.[[339]](#cite_note-Starfighter_Press-339) *Galactic Starfighter* was first conceived shortly after the release of *The Old Republic*, but before the developers could define what the expansion would actually look like, the project was put on hold in favor of additional content and the Free-to-Play system. It was not until August 2012 that the developers resumed work on identifying how they wanted to approach space content. Comments and requests by fans factored into the discussion, and the developers soon established two main factors: free-flight space combat and ship customization. The developers soon decided to pursue player-vs-player combat instead of developing a large open world with story content and massive capital ships, and work started on the expansion's development.[[340]](#cite_note-GSDev_Part_1-340)

Prior to the official announcement, *Galactic Starfighter* was teased as the "Super Secret Space Project." It was first mentioned in the second LiveStream Event on [November 29](/wiki/November_29 "November 29"), 2012, and was described as "something that is a departure from our normal space game."[[341]](#cite_note-Dulfy_Transcript-341) It was not mentioned again until August 2013, when a teaser video was shown at the Community Cantina Tour in Seattle. The video, framed as footage from a surveillance droid in space and an audio report by an agent of the Shroud addressed to the Shroud, describes the agent's findings that the Republic and the Empire are gathering their naval forces. A Republic fleet attacks an Imperial shipyard, and the video shows gameplay footage of [*Liberator*-class starfighters](/wiki/Liberator-class_starfighter "Liberator-class starfighter") and [Mark VI *Supremacy*-class starfighters](/wiki/Mark_VI_Supremacy-class_starfighter "Mark VI Supremacy-class starfighter") dogfighting before the surveillance droid is destroyed. No other information about the feature or its release date was announced during the Cantina Tour.[[342]](#cite_note-SSSP_Dulfy-342)

*Galactic Starfighter* is a Free-to-Play expansion that centers around the addition of player-vs-player space combat to the game. *Galactic Starfighter* features variety of unique starships divided into three types, customizations and upgrade options for those ships, and multiple gameplay modes and battle zones, including 12 v. 12 space battles. Early Access to *Galactic Starfighter* for active subscribers began on December 3, 2013[[339]](#cite_note-Starfighter_Press-339) when Game Update 2.5 went live,[[202]](#cite_note-Holiday_Update-202) and Preferred Status Players received it on [January 14](/wiki/January_14 "January 14"); the expansion was made available to Free-to-Play gamers on February 4. Subscribers also received exclusive paint jobs, two pilot suits, two titles, and the maximum leveling and progression benefit available—a benefit which can also be gained through the purchase of a Starfigher Pass in the Cartel Market. Preferred Status Players received two pilot suits and an exclusive title., and any player who was a subscriber by [November 1](/wiki/November_1 "November 1") received an exclusive Gunship unlock with custom paint jobs.[[339]](#cite_note-Starfighter_Press-339)

#### *Galactic Strongholds*

 [![Galactic Strongholds](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/8/8b/Galactic_Strongholds_Logo.png/revision/latest?cb=20151117045707) [![Galactic Strongholds](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/8/8b/Galactic_Strongholds_Logo.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/250?cb=20151117045707)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/8/8b/Galactic_Strongholds_Logo.png/revision/latest?cb=20151117045707) 

*Galactic Strongholds*

 

:   [![icon](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/04/Blue_Glass_Arrow.svg/revision/latest?cb=20090726033133) Main article: [Star Wars: The Old Republic: Galactic Strongholds](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Old_Republic:_Galactic_Strongholds "Star Wars: The Old Republic: Galactic Strongholds")

:   "*Have you ever dreamed of having a home in the* Star Wars*™ galaxy? I mean a real home – a place you can look forward to returning to after a long journey through the cold depths of space. A place that you can retreat to in times of darkness, to meditate on your next move or to plot your revenge. A place you can share with your closest friends or flaunt to your rivals. Above all, a place of power and significance that you can customize and call your own. We share that dream, and we intend to make it a reality with our next free digital expansion: **GALACTIC STRONGHOLDS***"
:   ―Jesse Sky[[117]](#cite_note-Developer_Update:_Strongholds_Introduction-117)

***Star Wars: The Old Republic: Galactic Strongholds*** is the third Digital Expansion for *Star Wars: The Old Republic*, and launched in late summer of 2014. The Digital Expansion was first mentioned in February in the developers' "road map" for 2014, and it was officially announced on [March 19](/wiki/March_19 "March 19"), 2014.[[70]](#cite_note-Road_Map_2014-70) *Galactic Strongholds* was preceded by a number of bonuses for existing subscribers and players who become subscribers by various dates in the months leading up to August.[[13]](#cite_note-Galactic_Strongholds-13) *Galactic Strongholds* was originally given an Early Access launch date of [June 24](/wiki/June_24 "June 24") for Subscribers and [July 29](/wiki/July_29 "July 29") for Preferred Status Players, and a Free-to-Play launch date of August.[[13]](#cite_note-Galactic_Strongholds-13) However, the expansion was delayed so that the development team could implement an array of additional features; the new Early Access date for Subscribers was [August 19](/wiki/August_19 "August 19"), Preferred Access on [September 16](/wiki/September_16 "September 16"), and the official launch on October 14.[[264]](#cite_note-Producer_Letter:_Galactic_Strongholds-264) The Digital Expansion allows players at level 15 and above[[117]](#cite_note-Developer_Update:_Strongholds_Introduction-117) to live on multiple planets and own their own apartment, or Stronghold.[[13]](#cite_note-Galactic_Strongholds-13)

Currently, four strongholds have been added: the Coruscant Skyrise Apartment, the Dromund Kaas Apartment, the Nar Shaddaa Sky Palace,[[13]](#cite_note-Galactic_Strongholds-13) and the Tatooine Homestead.[[116]](#cite_note-Galactic_Living_Tatooine_Homestead-116) All four can be owned by the same Legacy, and players can purchase and unlock decorations as they advance through the game; additional decorations will be added as rewards for elements such as Reputation, PvP, and Crew Skills. Players can give other players temporary invitations or permanent keys to visit their Stronghold, and can also post it on the Public Listing. Each decoration adds to a player's Legacy's Prestige score, and a new Legacy Storage feature will be available with the Strongholds.[[117]](#cite_note-Developer_Update:_Strongholds_Introduction-117) Guilds are also now able to use Guild Flagships where members can meet, and each week guilds can compete by completing Conquests missions to control planets for member perks.[[13]](#cite_note-Galactic_Strongholds-13) With the delayed launch, the development team added a number of features: a new Tatooine Homestead Stronghold, expanded functionality for Guild Flagships, new Conquest Events, and the ability to place vehicles, pets, and companion characters as decorations.[[264]](#cite_note-Producer_Letter:_Galactic_Strongholds-264)

#### Shadow of Revan

 [![Shadow of Revan](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/d/d4/Shadow_of_Revan_promo.png/revision/latest?cb=20141016013809) [![Shadow of Revan](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/d/d4/Shadow_of_Revan_promo.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/250?cb=20141016013809)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/d/d4/Shadow_of_Revan_promo.png/revision/latest?cb=20141016013809) 

*Shadow of Revan*

 

:   [![icon](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/04/Blue_Glass_Arrow.svg/revision/latest?cb=20090726033133) Main article: [Star Wars: The Old Republic: Shadow of Revan](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Old_Republic:_Shadow_of_Revan "Star Wars: The Old Republic: Shadow of Revan")

:   "*The Shadow of Revan Digital Expansion is the grand culmination of the Forged Alliances story arc. Revan is ready to make his boldest move yet, and we are excited to share it with you. When we started developing Shadow of Revan, we wanted to go back to our BioWare roots and focus on the story. We know that BioWare story is at the top of the list for things players want to experience in* Star Wars*™: The Old Republic™, and we think we've delivered that with Shadow of Revan. This expansion is the effort of a lot of dedicated work from people who care deeply about compelling narrative.*"
:   ―Andrew Horwitz[[269]](#cite_note-Shadow_Welcome-269)

***Star Wars: The Old Republic: Shadow of Revan*** is the fourth Digital Expansion for *The Old Republic*, and launched on [December 9](/wiki/December_9 "December 9"), 2014.[[14]](#cite_note-Shadow_of_Revan-14) On February 3, 2014, it was announced that players could expect two Digital Expansions in 2014, similar to the two released in 2013. The first, later announced to *Galactic Strongholds*, was said to resemble *Galactic Starfighter* in scope, while the second expansion was stated to be similar to *Rise of the Hutt Cartel*.[[70]](#cite_note-Road_Map_2014-70) The short teaser entitled "A Deadly Force Returns" was released on [September 16](/wiki/September_16 "September 16") and featured the returned Revan;[[343]](#cite_note-Returns-343) a full announcement was expected by the end of [September](/wiki/September "September")[[344]](#cite_note-Musco-344) after a brief trailer entitled "Revan Returns" was released on [September 16](/wiki/September_16 "September 16"), but was delayed until [October 6](/wiki/October_6 "October 6").[[14]](#cite_note-Shadow_of_Revan-14) The expansion is a continuation of the "Forged Alliances" three-part Flashpoint storyline, but completion of the "Forged Alliances" Flashpoints is not a requirement for the expansion;[[345]](#cite_note-The_Story_of_SWTOR,_2014-345) the expansion adds solo versions of the Forged Alliance Flashpoints so players can complete the storyline and also includes dialogue for players who have yet to complete Forged Alliances.[[56]](#cite_note-TORSOR-56)

As with *Rise of the Hutt Cartel*, *Shadow of Revan* was preceded by a number of pre-order bonuses, and it was released alongside Game Update 3.0 on [December 2](/wiki/December_2 "December 2"). The actual expansion was be released to the public on [December 9](/wiki/December_9 "December 9"), though players who pre-ordered *Shadow of Revan* prior to [November 2](/wiki/November_2 "November 2") received a week of Early Access starting on December 2, in addition to an exclusive Grand Statue of Revan and the *Rise of Hutt Cartel* expansion for free. Players who purchased before December 1 also received the statue and *Rise of the Hutt Cartel*, and subscribers who pre-ordered the expansion received a Class Experience Boost that rewards players with a 12x boost to experience gained in class missions; the boost was effective from the moment the expansion was purchased until December 1.[[14]](#cite_note-Shadow_of_Revan-14) *Shadow of Revan* introduces two new worlds—Yavin 4 and Rishi—as well as two Flashpoints and two Operations, and raises the level cap another five levels to 60. Additionally, four Hard Modes were added for existing Flashpoints. Unlike previous expansions, *Shadow of Revan* also included eight class-exclusive missions, one for each class, that tie into the expansion's primary storyline faction storylines. The class missions serve as interludes during the Rishi storyline, and the ending cutscenes for the expansion advance each class's storyline in unique ways.[[56]](#cite_note-TORSOR-56)

#### *Knights of the Fallen Empire*

 [![Knights of the Fallen Empire](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/e/ef/Knights_of_the_Fallen_Empire_logo.png/revision/latest?cb=20151117051458) [![Knights of the Fallen Empire](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/e/ef/Knights_of_the_Fallen_Empire_logo.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/250?cb=20151117051458)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/e/ef/Knights_of_the_Fallen_Empire_logo.png/revision/latest?cb=20151117051458) 

*Knights of the Fallen Empire*

 

:   [![icon](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/04/Blue_Glass_Arrow.svg/revision/latest?cb=20090726033133) Main article: [Star Wars: The Old Republic: Knights of the Fallen Empire](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Old_Republic:_Knights_of_the_Fallen_Empire "Star Wars: The Old Republic: Knights of the Fallen Empire")

***Star Wars: The Old Republic: Knights of the Fallen Empire*** is the fifth Digital Expansion for *The Old Republic*. First mentioned on [June 12](/wiki/June_12 "June 12"), [2015](/wiki/2015 "2015") in advance of [Electronic Arts](/wiki/Electronic_Arts "Electronic Arts")'s official presentations at the 2015 Electronic Entertainment Expo on [June 15](/wiki/June_15 "June 15"), *Knights of the Fallen Empire* was said to feature a renewed focus on cinematic storytelling, as well as new worlds, new companions, and a dynamic story that will be affected by the choices players make. The expansion was first hinted at in the Community Cantina Tour held in Anaheim, California on [April 18](/wiki/April_18 "April 18"); wristbands were given out that featured the hashtag #FallenEmpire and the date "06.15.15," and a secret image featuring a throne and the hashtag was hidden in the files given to attendees and later posted online.[[273]](#cite_note-EA-273)

The Digital Expansion was released on [October 20](/wiki/October_20 "October 20"), 2015, along with Game Update 4.0 which added new companions, the new planet [Zakuul](/wiki/Zakuul "Zakuul") and a revamp of all the old Flashpoints and Operations, along with the new Flashpoint: Star Fortress. The update also raised the level cap from 50 to 65 and gave subscribers the ability to start their games at level 60. *Knights of the Fallen Empire* features nine new chapters, with additional chapters being released throughout Early [2016](/wiki/2016 "2016").[[93]](#cite_note-Update_4.0-93) The expansion focuses on the new threat of [Emperor](/wiki/Emperor/Legends "Emperor/Legends") [Valkorion](/wiki/Tenebrae "Tenebrae") and his [Eternal Empire](/wiki/Eternal_Empire "Eternal Empire"). At Level 60, the player is frozen in [carbonite](/wiki/Carbonite/Legends "Carbonite/Legends") and awakens five years later, in [3632 BBY](/wiki/3632_BBY "3632 BBY"), to find that the galaxy is ruled by the Eternal Empire. The player, now called the "Outlander" has to find allies and stop and defeat the Eternal Empire.

#### *Knights of the Eternal Throne*

 [![Knights of the Eternal Throne](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/a/a0/Knights_of_the_Eternal_Throne_logo.png/revision/latest?cb=20160722222049) [![Knights of the Eternal Throne](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/a/a0/Knights_of_the_Eternal_Throne_logo.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/250?cb=20160722222049)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/a/a0/Knights_of_the_Eternal_Throne_logo.png/revision/latest?cb=20160722222049) 

*Knights of the Eternal Throne*

 

:   [![icon](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/04/Blue_Glass_Arrow.svg/revision/latest?cb=20090726033133) Main article: [Star Wars: The Old Republic: Knights of the Eternal Throne](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Old_Republic:_Knights_of_the_Eternal_Throne "Star Wars: The Old Republic: Knights of the Eternal Throne")

***Star Wars: The Old Republic: Knights of the Eternal Throne*** is the sixth Digital Expansion for *The Old Republic*. Revealed at the EA *Star Wars* "Meet the Makers" panel at [Celebration Europe 2016](/wiki/Celebration_Europe_(2016) "Celebration Europe (2016)"), the expansion was released in fall of 2016, in celebration of the game's five-year anniversary.[[346]](#cite_note-KotET_Announce-346)

#### *Onslaught*

 [![Onslaught](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/f/ff/Onslaught_Key_Art.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20200511151813) [![Onslaught](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/f/ff/Onslaught_Key_Art.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/250?cb=20200511151813)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/f/ff/Onslaught_Key_Art.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20200511151813) 

*Onslaught*

 

:   [![icon](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/04/Blue_Glass_Arrow.svg/revision/latest?cb=20090726033133) Main article: [Star Wars: The Old Republic: Onslaught](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Old_Republic:_Onslaught "Star Wars: The Old Republic: Onslaught")

***Star Wars: The Old Republic: Onslaught*** is the seventh Digital Expansion for *The Old Republic*. The expansion was first announced at the Community Cantina Tour held in Chicago, Illinois on [April 13](/wiki/April_13 "April 13"), [2019](/wiki/2019 "2019"). The expansion was released on [October 22](/wiki/October_22 "October 22"), [2019](/wiki/2019 "2019").[[16]](#cite_note-OnsAnnouncement-16)

#### *Legacy of the Sith*

 [![Legacy of the Sith](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/01/TORLegacyoftheSith-KeyArt.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20220303222845) [![Legacy of the Sith](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/01/TORLegacyoftheSith-KeyArt.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/250?cb=20220303222845)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/01/TORLegacyoftheSith-KeyArt.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20220303222845) 

*Legacy of the Sith*

 

:   [![icon](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/04/Blue_Glass_Arrow.svg/revision/latest?cb=20090726033133) Main article: [Star Wars: The Old Republic: Legacy of the Sith](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Old_Republic:_Legacy_of_the_Sith "Star Wars: The Old Republic: Legacy of the Sith")

***Star Wars: The Old Republic: Legacy of the Sith*** is the eighth Digital Expansion for *The Old Republic*. The expansion was first announced on July 1, 2021 in celebration of the game's tenth-year anniversary. The expansion introduced combat styles, a new feature that allowed players to choose a specific class story and combine it with ability sets from other related classes. The expansion also featured a new revamped character creation system, along with a new look for the character sheet.[[17]](#cite_note-LotSAnnouncement-17) The cinematic trailer, titled *[Disorder](/wiki/Disorder "Disorder")*, was released alongside the expansion and serves as a trailer for *Legacy of the Sith*. The expansion was released on February 15, 2022.[[347]](#cite_note-DisorderTrailer-347)

## Release and reception

As of 2011, the game and its trailers have won a total of 85 awards from various industry critics and organizations over the course of 2009–2011. Many of the awards were in response to *The Old Republic*'s cinematic game trailers and gameplay presentations at E3; some awards won in 2011 included Best MMO from IncGamers and GamePro, Best PC Game from Machinima, and Most Valuable Game from PC Gamer.[[348]](#cite_note-Awards-348) In 2012, [The AbleGamers Foundation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_AbleGamers_Foundation "wikipedia:The AbleGamers Foundation") declared *The Old Republic* their Mainstream Game of 2011 because of the game's ability to accommodate gamers with special needs. The Foundation praised the accessibility options in the game's features, including subtitles, queueable actions, multiple action bars, and built-in mouse sensitivity, as well as auto-looting and area looting.[[349]](#cite_note-AbleGamers-349)

## Continuity

### References to other works

 [![The head of Darth Bandon](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/5/52/PickledSith-TORCodex.png/revision/latest?cb=20140808130035) [![The head of Darth Bandon](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/5/52/PickledSith-TORCodex.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/170?cb=20140808130035)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/5/52/PickledSith-TORCodex.png/revision/latest?cb=20140808130035) 

The head of Darth Bandon

 

:   "*You must understand, the head of Darth Bandon is a priceless artifact. He was the Sith Lord who murdered one of Alderaan's noblest sons. Centuries ago, Trask Ulgo bravely sacrificed himself in combat with Darth Bandon. Trask's martyrdom saved the Galactic Republic. […] Trask's death was a noble sacrifice. It allowed a powerful Force user to live who eventually went on to destroy the evil Darth Malak.*"
:   ―Peema Ahuff[[9]](#cite_note-Manual-9)

As the successor to BioWare's *Knights of the Old Republic* and *Knights of the Old Republic II: The Sith Lords*, *The Old Republic* borrows heavily from the content of those two games, as well as the [*Tales of the Jedi*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Tales_of_the_Jedi_(comic_series) "Star Wars: Tales of the Jedi (comic series)") and [*Knights of the Old Republic*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Knights_of_the_Old_Republic_(comic_series) "Star Wars: Knights of the Old Republic (comic series)") comic series. *The Old Republic* is set three hundred years after the two *KOTOR* games, and the planet of Taris—which was destroyed in the beginning of *Knights of the Old Republic*—is gradually recovering from the destruction. The *Endar Spire*, the starting ship for the first game, can be found on Taris's surface where it crashed following the beginning of the game. The rakghoul creatures from *Knights of the Old Republic* are present, and several side missions in *The Old Republic* tie in to optional side quests from *Knights of the Old Republic*, confirming the outcomes of the original quests as canon. Similar to Taris, the planet Alderaan is home to numerous references to other continuity: the Alderaanian noble House Ulgo includes the character [Trask Ulgo](/wiki/Trask_Ulgo "Trask Ulgo") from *Knights of the Old Republic*,[[350]](#cite_note-KOTOR-350) and the insectoid Killiks as well as Houses Organa and Thul are all elements that have been part of *Star Wars* canon for over a decade.[[351]](#cite_note-Dark_Nest-351)

The Sith Empire present in *The Old Republic* is established by the survivors of the Great Hyperspace War, the conflict depicted in [*Tales of the Jedi: The Fall of the Sith Empire*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Tales_of_the_Jedi_%E2%80%93_The_Fall_of_the_Sith_Empire "Star Wars: Tales of the Jedi – The Fall of the Sith Empire"),[[352]](#cite_note-Timeline_11-352) and both the planet Korriban and the Sith Inquisitor storyline include major characters and elements from [*Tales of the Jedi: The Golden Age of the Sith*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Tales_of_the_Jedi_%E2%80%93_The_Golden_Age_of_the_Sith "Star Wars: Tales of the Jedi – The Golden Age of the Sith") and *The Fall of the Sith Empire*, such as Horak-mul, Naga Sadow, and Marka Ragnos.[[353]](#cite_note-Tales-353) The various tie-in materials—the novels, comics, Timeline videos, and other content—describe the backstory of the galactic powers and the game's conflict, and several major characters from *The Old Republic* are introduced in the comics and novels: Satele Shan, Darth Baras, Orgus Din, Darth Angral, Braden, Darth Thanaton, Jaric Kaedan, Elin Garza, Nasan Godera, Bela Kiwiiks, and Darth Marr are among the major characters that originated outside of the game itself.[[139]](#cite_note-Threat_of_Peace-139)[[149]](#cite_note-Blood_of_the_Empire-149)[[354]](#cite_note-Lost_Suns-354)

The "True Sith" that [Kreia](/wiki/Kreia "Kreia") describes in *The Sith Lords* are established to the reconstituted Sith Empire, and the tie-in novel *The Old Republic: Revan* bridges the gaps between *Knights of the Old Republic*, *The Sith Lords*, and *The Old Republic*, explaining what happened to Revan and Meetra Surik—the protagonists of the first two games—and how they end up appearing in *The Old Republic*.[[167]](#cite_note-TOR:_Revan-167) Revan himself receives a multitude of references throughout *The Old Republic*: [Revan's Cross of Glory](/wiki/Revan%27s_Cross_of_Glory "Revan's Cross of Glory"), a [complex](/wiki/Darth_Revan%27s_complex "Darth Revan's complex") on Nar Shaddaa established by Revan, [Revan's mask](/wiki/Revan%27s_mask "Revan's mask"), and the Order of Revan are just some of the references to the Jedi Master within *The Old Republic*. Revan himself appears in the game, serving as the focus of four interconnected Flashpoints that also include an appearance by Meetra Surik's Force ghost and a Rakatan space station known as the Foundry, a station similar to the [Star Forge](/wiki/Star_Forge "Star Forge") of *Knights of the Old Republic*.[[24]](#cite_note-TOR-24)

 [![The Noetikon Jedi, among them , , Arca Jeth, Bastila Shan, , and ](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/8/8c/Noetikon_Jedi.png/revision/latest?cb=20130811000810) [![The Noetikon Jedi, among them , , Arca Jeth, Bastila Shan, , and ](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/8/8c/Noetikon_Jedi.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/200?cb=20130811000810)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/8/8c/Noetikon_Jedi.png/revision/latest?cb=20130811000810) 

The Noetikon Jedi, among them [Nomi Sunrider](/wiki/Nomi_Sunrider "Nomi Sunrider"), [Noab Hulis](/wiki/Noab_Hulis "Noab Hulis"), Arca Jeth, Bastila Shan, [Vandar Tokare](/wiki/Vandar_Tokare "Vandar Tokare"), and [Chamma](/wiki/Chamma "Chamma")

 

The character of Satele Shan, the Jedi Grand Master, was first introduced in the *Threat of Peace* webcomics, and she is the descendant of Revan and the companion character Bastila Shan from *Knights of the Old Republic*.[[139]](#cite_note-Threat_of_Peace-139) The Noetikons, holocron-like devices that appear in the Jedi Consular storyline, feature a number of characters from *Tales of the Jedi* and *Knights of the Old Republic*, though some characters, such as Arca Jeth and Bastila Shan, feature altered character models because of differences in graphics.[[24]](#cite_note-TOR-24) *The Old Republic*'s metaseries also retcons the story behind Revan and Malak's fall to the dark side, establishing that they were corrupted by the Sith Emperor and sent back to the Republic as his agents before they broke free from the Emperor's mental control.[[167]](#cite_note-TOR:_Revan-167) The Republic Fleet hub Carrick Station is a reference to Zayne Carrick, the protagonist of the *Knights of the Old Republic* comics series,[[24]](#cite_note-TOR-24) and the two ships in the hub—the [*Gav Daragon*](/wiki/Gav_Daragon_(Valor-class) "Gav Daragon (Valor-class)") and the [*Telos*](/wiki/Telos_(Valor-class) "Telos (Valor-class)")—are callbacks to the *Tales of the Jedi* [character](/wiki/Gav_Daragon "Gav Daragon")[[353]](#cite_note-Tales-353) and the [planet](/wiki/Telos_IV "Telos IV") in *The Sith Lords*.[[355]](#cite_note-KOTOR_2-355)

*The Old Republic* features an in-game Codex, a database of information on the *Star Wars* universe, whose entries are unlocked through various quests, exploration, and discovering attribute-boosting datacrons. Each datacron unlocks one of almost 90 Galactic History entries, which cover the history of the galaxy from the [Celestials](/wiki/Celestial/Legends "Celestial/Legends") to the end of the Great Galactic War. Through the Galactic History entries, *The Old Republic* effectively summarizes most of the content that has been introduced in that span of time, covering previously established continuity while also expanding on lesser-known points and introducing new content. Other entries in the Codex also give background on various locations, species, characters, items, and events in the game, summarizing preexisting information and establishing new content.[[156]](#cite_note-Developer_Blog:_Introducing_the_Codex-156)

The Crewskill system, particularly the mission crewskills, is a major source of references to older continuity. Events, characters, and locations from Tales of the Jedi and the *Knights of the Old Republic* games and comics, such as the bombing of Socorro, the attack on Dantooine, the Telos Academy, the destruction of Peragus, the companion character Mical, and the Mandalorian scientist Demagol are referenced in the Crewskill missions, which borrow from all manner of sources in the Expanded Universe. Planets, locations, and cultures from a wide variety of sourcebooks, novels, comics, and other materials are touched upon, and the game also introduces a large number of locations and characters to canon through the Crewskill missions.[[97]](#cite_note-Holonet_Crew_Skills-97)

Many of the planets in *The Old Republic* originated in prior sources, and some had never been visually depicted before. The planet Belsavis was first introduced in the 1995 novel *Children of the Jedi*, but aside from scattered mentions, the planet was largely undescribed in pre-existing continuity. The designers chose to use Belsavis after coming across the planet in the Holocron, and they expanded on the description of Belsavis as an ice world with rifts in its surface that were home to jungle areas warmed by volcanic vents.[[49]](#cite_note-Art-49) The planet Oricon, which is a Daily Mission Area in Update 2.4, was only mentioned in a [web enhancement](/wiki/Behind_the_Threat:_The_Sith "Behind the Threat: The Sith") for the *[Star Wars Roleplaying Game](/wiki/Star_Wars_Roleplaying_Game "Star Wars Roleplaying Game")* by [Wizards of the Coast](/wiki/Wizards_of_the_Coast "Wizards of the Coast"),[[356]](#cite_note-Oricon_Wizards-356) and Ord Mantell and Tython had been mentioned or appeared frequently in various novels but had never been visually depicted to the extent they are in *The Old Republic*.[[49]](#cite_note-Art-49)

The planet Deralia, which was originally mentioned in *Knights of the Old Republic*, saw its first appearance in a Jedi Consular class mission,[[24]](#cite_note-TOR-24) and the Gree world of Asation originated in a [HoloNet News](/wiki/HoloNet_News/Legends "HoloNet News/Legends") issue that was released in [2002](/wiki/2002 "2002") as a tie-in to [*Star Wars*: Episode II *Attack of the Clones*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_II_Attack_of_the_Clones "Star Wars: Episode II Attack of the Clones").[[357]](#cite_note-Asation_Holonet-357) Saleucami, Chandrila, and the Tion Hegemony are all locales that have previously appeared in *Star Wars* content, and the planet of Athiss was previously only mentioned in the *[Tales of the Jedi Companion](/wiki/Tales_of_the_Jedi_Companion "Tales of the Jedi Companion")* sourcebook.[[358]](#cite_note-Tales_Companion-358) The planets Quesh and Voss, however, are entirely new planets in *Star Wars* continuity,[[49]](#cite_note-Art-49) and a number of other planets that appear in Flashpoints, Operations, and class missions—including Zadd, Darvannis, and Denova—were created for *The Old Republic* as well.[[24]](#cite_note-TOR-24) The *Shadow of Revan* Digital Expansion added the moon Yavin 4, which appeared in both *A New Hope* and the *Tales of the Jedi* series, and the pirate haven [Rishi](/wiki/Rishi/Legends "Rishi/Legends"), which has received mentions and appearances in material since the early days of the Expanded Universe.[[14]](#cite_note-Shadow_of_Revan-14)

### Contradictions and errors

:   "*This map was a bear. You'll find lots of little islands of exploration and odd peninsulas to reflect the fact that so many worlds we were once told were charted, founded or settled late in galactic history have shown up in the eras explored by the various* Knights of the Old Republic *tales. In the final days of work on the Atlas, a good chunk of 'blue' space had to be hastily turned turquoise to account for two things: the forthcoming* The Old Republic *MMO and its new origin story for the Hydian Way, and the mention of the Minos Cluster in an online comic connected to the game.*"
:   ―Jason Fry, on the Galactic Explorations map[[359]](#cite_note-Wallace_Endnotes-359)

With the number of references to other continuity in *The Old Republic*, there have been some errors and conflicting details. One of the issues is the planet Hoth, which is the site of a large ship graveyard and a significant number of military structures; some fans argued it should not have been included because it was largely unexplored before the [Battle of Hoth](/wiki/Battle_of_Hoth/Legends "Battle of Hoth/Legends") in [3 ABY](/wiki/3_ABY/Legends "3 ABY/Legends").[[360]](#cite_note-360)[[361]](#cite_note-361) In *Knights of the Old Republic*, the *Endar Spire* explodes just after Revan and Carth Onasi escape,[[350]](#cite_note-KOTOR-350) but the ship appears largely intact on the surface of Taris in *The Old Republic*. Similarly, the character Brejik in *Knights of the Old Republic* is a hostile swoop rider who is killed by the player shortly before the bombardment of Taris,[[350]](#cite_note-KOTOR-350) but *The Old Republic*'s Codex introduces a swoop rider named [Milos Brejik](/wiki/Milos_Brejik "Milos Brejik") who survived the bombardment and helped other survivors scavenge food.[[362]](#cite_note-Brejik's_Run-362)

*The Old Republic* also includes the Chiss species, a culture from the Unknown Regions that had previously been established as isolationist and largely unknown to the galaxy, and the Sith Empire is allies with the Chiss Ascendancy.[[363]](#cite_note-Chiss-363) The layout of the Valley of the Dark Lords on the planet Korriban is significantly different than how it appears in the *Knights of the Old Republic* games, though the games themselves conflict with *Tales of the Jedi*, the novel *[Darth Bane: Path of Destruction](/wiki/Darth_Bane:_Path_of_Destruction "Darth Bane: Path of Destruction")*, the video game *[Star Wars: Jedi Knight: Jedi Academy](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Jedi_Knight:_Jedi_Academy "Star Wars: Jedi Knight: Jedi Academy")*, and various other sources. There is a further discrepancy between *Knights of the Old Republic* and *The Old Republic* in one of the Taris side missions: the Outcast Rukil stated that it would take weeks or months to reach the [Promised Land](/wiki/Promised_Land "Promised Land") from the Taris [Undercity](/wiki/Undercity_(Taris) "Undercity (Taris)"), but *The Old Republic* reveals that the Outcasts made it to the Promised Land before the bombardment of Taris.[[350]](#cite_note-KOTOR-350)

*The Old Republic* was the first *Star Wars* product to touch upon the origin of the Jedi Order in any specific fashion, establishing the characters of [Garon Jard](/wiki/Garon_Jard "Garon Jard"), Rajivari, [Ters Sendon](/wiki/Ters_Sendon "Ters Sendon"), and [Cala Brin](/wiki/Cala_Brin "Cala Brin") as the members of the first Jedi Council and describing the Force Wars as a conflict between the Jedi and Rajivari's followers. However, the comic series *[Star Wars: Dawn of the Jedi](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Dawn_of_the_Jedi "Star Wars: Dawn of the Jedi")*, which is set in the [Before the Republic](/wiki/Before_the_Republic "Before the Republic") publishing era and deals with the Je'daii Order—the Jedi Order's predecessors—began shortly after the release of *The Old Republic*, and it presented a largely different origin of the Jedi, with the Je'daii Order developing a philosophy of balance between the light and dark sides, and their [Je'daii Council](/wiki/Je%27daii_Council "Je'daii Council") did not include any of the characters introduced in *The Old Republic*.[[364]](#cite_note-DOTJ_1-364) The [sixth issue](/wiki/Dawn_of_the_Jedi:_The_Prisoner_of_Bogan_1 "Dawn of the Jedi: The Prisoner of Bogan 1") of *Dawn of the Jedi* featured an appearance by Rajivari, starting the process of reconciling the two conflicting sources,[[365]](#cite_note-DOTJ_6-365) and the [*Force War*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Dawn_of_the_Jedi:_Force_War "Star Wars: Dawn of the Jedi: Force War") arc revealed that the Flesh Raiders were in fact mutated Rakata used as soldiers, explaining how they arrived on Tython.[[366]](#cite_note-Force_War-366)

A further contradiction between *Dawn of the Jedi* and *The Old Republic* deals with the origin of several species, including Twi'leks and Zabraks. The Rakatan device known as [Mother Machine](/wiki/Mother_Machine "Mother Machine") on Belsavis identified itself as being responsible for the creation of the Twi'leks, Zabraks, [Esh-kha](/wiki/Esh-kha "Esh-kha"), and other species in an effort to restore the Force-sensitivity of the Rakatan species as the Infinite Empire collapsed. However, *Dawn of the Jedi* contradicts the Mother Machine, showing an advanced Twi'lek civilization on their homeworld of [Ryloth](/wiki/Ryloth/Legends "Ryloth/Legends") as well as a pre-existing Zabrak species in [36,453 BBY](/wiki/36,453_BBY "36,453 BBY"), thousands of years before the Infinite Empire's collapse.[[364]](#cite_note-DOTJ_1-364) The 2010 novel [*Red Harvest*](/wiki/Red_Harvest_(novel) "Red Harvest (novel)") by [Joe Schreiber](/wiki/Joe_Schreiber "Joe Schreiber"), a prequel to his earlier novel *[Death Troopers](/wiki/Death_Troopers "Death Troopers")*, is stated to occur in the year [3645 BBY](/wiki/3645_BBY "3645 BBY"), shortly before the events of *The Old Republic*. However, the novel makes very little mention of the Great Galactic War, the Cold War, or any of the other events or backstory from *The Old Republic*, and the character [Hestizo Trace](/wiki/Hestizo_Trace "Hestizo Trace") makes a mention of an intact Jedi Temple on Coruscant—eight years after the Temple's destruction and during a time period in which the Jedi Order had relocated to Tython.[[367]](#cite_note-Red_Harvest-367)

*The Old Republic: Fatal Alliance* was released early in the development of *The Old Republic*, and as a result the novel is not based on the finalized version of the game's setting. Almost all of the game's characters, events, and other elements have been virtually ignored by *The Old Republic* and all other material in the metaseries, and conflicts have arisen between the novel and the game. Three of the four Jedi Council members introduced in the novel—[Wens Aleusis](/wiki/Wens_Aleusis "Wens Aleusis"), [Nikil Nobil](/wiki/Nikil_Nobil "Nikil Nobil"), and [Giffis Fane](/wiki/Giffis_Fane "Giffis Fane")—have been effectively ignored by *The Old Republic*, which introduced an entirely new Council; however, the Assault on Tython Flashpoint in Game Update 2.7 featured the fourth Council member, Oric Traless, as a boss. Satele Shan's Padawan [Shigar Konshi](/wiki/Shigar_Konshi "Shigar Konshi") and the novel's other main characters, excluding the Grand Master herself, have yet to be involved or even appear outside of *Fatal Alliance*. The novel also introduces the [Duros](/wiki/Duros/Legends "Duros/Legends") Supreme Commander [Stantorrs](/wiki/Stantorrs "Stantorrs"), but *The Old Republic* directly contradicts Stantorrs' existence by stating that the Human Rans has been Supreme Commander since the beginning of the Great War.[[151]](#cite_note-Fatal_Alliance-151)

However, some elements from *Fatal Alliance* have been retained: Elin Garza was briefly mentioned in the novel, and both the Justicars' Brigade and Larin Moxla's former unit, [Blackstar Squad](/wiki/Blackstar_Squad "Blackstar Squad"), make appearances in the game.[[24]](#cite_note-TOR-24) The *Star Wars: The Old Republic Encyclopedia* attempted to reconcile the different compositions of the Jedi Council by establishing that there were twelve members, which allowed the four Council members introduced in *Fatal Alliance* to be members of the Council at the same time as those who appeared in *The Old Republic*.[[23]](#cite_note-Encyclopedia-23) *Fatal Alliance* featured a ship named the "Kuat D7," a designation that ultimately became the *D5-Mantis* Patrol Craft produced by Kuat Drive Yards that serves as the player ship for the Bounty Hunter class. The novel also mentioned "B-28s,"[[151]](#cite_note-Fatal_Alliance-151) a starfighter whose name eventually became the [B28 *Extinction*-class bomber](/wiki/B28_Extinction-class_bomber "B28 Extinction-class bomber").[[368]](#cite_note-Archon-368) Similarly, *The Old Republic: Deceived* introduced the Corellian XS freighter, as well as the "BT7 Thunderstrike"—an early name for the Trooper class's BT-7 *Thunderclap*.[[155]](#cite_note-Deceived-155)

The Republic engineer [Lem Karner](/wiki/Lem_Karner "Lem Karner") states that he served on the front lines at the Battle of Bothawui, of which there were two during the Great Galactic War. The [first battle](/wiki/First_Battle_of_Bothawui "First Battle of Bothawui") was a strictly naval engagement, but the [second battle](/wiki/Battle_of_Bothawui_(Second;_Great_Galactic_War) "Battle of Bothawui (Second; Great Galactic War)"), while a ground engagement, ended with no Republic survivors. To date, it has not been identified which battle Lem Karner served in.[[24]](#cite_note-TOR-24) *The Journal of Master Gnost-Dural* establishes the date of the Battle of Hoth as 3665 BBY, in the middle of the Great Galactic War. However, the Imperial Agent storyline involving the Shadow Arsenal erroneously claims that the Battle of Hoth occurred at the end of the war by placing Colonel Laren Omas's death—which occurred during the battle—at the very end of the war. The Agent storyline also uses an Imperial transport as the Republic officer's shuttle, the *Starbreeze*. In *The Old Republic*, the companion character T7-O1 claims that he was constructed 150 years earlier,[[24]](#cite_note-TOR-24) but T7's Holonet entry and the *Star Wars: The Old Republic Encyclopedia* both contradict this, stating that he has been active for over two hundred years.[[23]](#cite_note-Encyclopedia-23) The [Arkanian](/wiki/Arkanian/Legends "Arkanian/Legends") Jedi Arca Jeth appears in hologram form in *The Old Republic*, but his appearance is that of a Human, as there is no character model for an Arkanian in the game.[[24]](#cite_note-TOR-24)

 [![A map of galactic exploration. Several blue parts of the map (explored between 5000 and 3000 BBY) were made turquoise (3000&ndash;1000 BBY) to account for The Old Republic.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/a/a6/GalacticExplorations.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20090903055148) [![A map of galactic exploration. Several blue parts of the map (explored between 5000 and 3000 BBY) were made turquoise (3000&ndash;1000 BBY) to account for The Old Republic.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/a/a6/GalacticExplorations.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/200?cb=20090903055148)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/a/a6/GalacticExplorations.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20090903055148) 

A map of galactic exploration. Several blue parts of the map (explored between 5000 and 3000 BBY) were made turquoise (3000–1000 BBY) to account for *The Old Republic*.

 

The Hydian Way had previously been established to have been charted by [Freia Kallea](/wiki/Freia_Kallea/Legends "Freia Kallea/Legends") around [3000 BBY](/wiki/3000_BBY "3000 BBY"),[[369]](#cite_note-Essential_Chronology-369) but this date was pushed back to around [3700 BBY](/wiki/3700_BBY/Legends "3700 BBY/Legends") for *The Old Republic* so BioWare could use the hyperlane. [Daniel Wallace](/wiki/Daniel_Wallace "Daniel Wallace") and [Jason Fry](/wiki/Jason_Fry "Jason Fry"), the authors of the 2009 reference guide *[The Essential Atlas](/wiki/The_Essential_Atlas "The Essential Atlas")*, learned of the retcon late in the publication process, but they were able to accommodate the change by altering the dates in the *Atlas*'s section on the founding of the Hydian Way. Also, the *Atlas*'s map of galactic explorations had to be revised, with sections of the galaxy changed from having been explored[[359]](#cite_note-Wallace_Endnotes-359) between 3000–[1000 BBY](/wiki/1000_BBY/Legends "1000 BBY/Legends") to between [5000](/wiki/5000_BBY/Legends "5000 BBY/Legends")–3000 BBY instead,[[370]](#cite_note-Atlas-370) allowing planets in those regions to be used in the game.[[359]](#cite_note-Wallace_Endnotes-359)

Certain entries of the game's Codex contradict pre-existing continuity, though only in minor details. The Codex entry "Galactic History 07: The First Spaceflights" states that Coruscant did not send out any colonists until the collapse of the Infinite Empire,[[371]](#cite_note-History_7-371) but previous sources have established that the Humans sent out a number of colony ships that settled worlds such as Alderaan, Corellia, and the Tion Hegemony hundreds of years before the Empire's collapse.[[370]](#cite_note-Atlas-370) "Galactic History 19: The Pius Dea Crusades" claims that the [Pius Dea](/wiki/Pius_Dea "Pius Dea")'s rule came to an end when a new Chancellor was elected,[[372]](#cite_note-History_19-372) but the [Pius Dea Era](/wiki/Pius_Dea_Era "Pius Dea Era") actually ended with the [Seventh Alsakan Conflict](/wiki/Seventh_Alsakan_Conflict "Seventh Alsakan Conflict"), which was followed by the Jedi Council's installment of Grand Master [Biel Ductavis](/wiki/Biel_Ductavis "Biel Ductavis") as Chancellor. However, Ductavis was not introduced until the release of *[The Essential Guide to Warfare](/wiki/The_Essential_Guide_to_Warfare "The Essential Guide to Warfare")* in April 2012, which ignored the Codex's account of the Pius Dea in favor of a new story.[[373]](#cite_note-Warfare-373)

The Codex entry "Galactic History 03: The Battalions of Zhell" erroneously claimed that the [Zhell](/wiki/Zhell/Legends "Zhell/Legends"), the precursor Human species, banded together into the [Battalions of Zhell](/wiki/Battalions_of_Zhell "Battalions of Zhell") after they were attacked by the rival [Taung](/wiki/Taung/Legends "Taung/Legends") species following an enormous volcanic eruption,[[374]](#cite_note-History_3-374) when in fact the Zhell were united and were fighting the Taung well before the volcano's eruption.[[373]](#cite_note-Warfare-373) The Codex entry "Galactic History 31: The Ritual of Nathema" discusses the [Ritual of Nathema](/wiki/Ritual_of_Nathema "Ritual of Nathema"), an event that first appeared in *The Old Republic Revan*, but claims that the event was celebrated by Imperial historians.[[375]](#cite_note-History_31-375) *The Old Republic: Revan* contradicts this, stating that the Emperor erased all mentions of his homeworld from Imperial history to conceal how he gained his power.[[167]](#cite_note-TOR:_Revan-167) When the character of Darth Acina was introduced in *Rise of the Hutt Cartel*, her Codex entry originally stated that she was the successor to Darth Hadra as head of the Sphere of Technology. However, the novel *The Old Republic: Annihilation*, which was released prior to *Rise of the Hutt Cartel*, had already established Darth Karrid as Hadra's successor.[[27]](#cite_note-Annihilation-27) This error was pointed on the forums of *The Old Republic*'s website to the writers, and Charles Boyd ensured in the next patch that the Codex entry was corrected to say Karrid instead of Hadra.[[376]](#cite_note-Incorrect_Codex_Entry_Forum-376)

## Legacy

The TV show [*The Big Bang Theory*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Big_Bang_Theory "wikipedia:The Big Bang Theory") featured *The Old Republic* in the episode "The Weekend Vortex" on [March 8](/wiki/March_8 "March 8"), 2012, where the show's four main characters spend the weekend playing *The Old Republic*. The episode showed clips of the game itself, and the show often has a copy of *The Old Republic: Revan* visible in the background of the set.[[377]](#cite_note-Big_Bang-377) Several LEGO sets based on *The Old Republic* have also been produced: one features a *Fury*-class Imperial interceptor and includes Darth Malgus with two Sith troopers,[[378]](#cite_note-Fury_LEGO-378) and a second features a *Liberator*-class starfighter—referred to as a "Republic Striker Starfighter"—with minifigures of Satele Shan, Jace Malcom, and T7-O1.[[379]](#cite_note-Striker_LEGO-379) A "battle pack" including a speeder, several Imperial troopers, and several Republic soldiers has been released,[[380]](#cite_note-Trooper_LEGO-380) and the most recent set has been a *Defender*-class light corvette—described as a "Jedi *Defender*-class Cruiser"—that includes a Sith Warrior, Kao Cen Darach, a Sith trooper, and a Mirialan Jedi Consular.[[381]](#cite_note-Defender_LEGO-381)

## Adaptations and tie-in media

### Short stories

#### Smuggler's Vanguard

[![Hylo-TORSV](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/5/5b/Hylo-TORSV.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20100325234653)

:   [![icon](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/04/Blue_Glass_Arrow.svg/revision/latest?cb=20090726033133) Main article: [The Old Republic: Smuggler's Vanguard](/wiki/The_Old_Republic:_Smuggler%27s_Vanguard "The Old Republic: Smuggler's Vanguard")

**"The Old Republic: Smuggler's Vanguard"** is a short story by Robert Chestney that was released exclusively on [StarWars.com](/wiki/StarWars.com "StarWars.com") on March 25, 2010,[[382]](#cite_note-Vanguard_SW-382) though it was republished on October 1 on the [Del Rey](/wiki/Del_Rey "Del Rey") website.[[383]](#cite_note-Vanguard_Suv-383) Set approximately [3660 BBY](/wiki/3660_BBY "3660 BBY"),[[384]](#cite_note-ERC-384) the story focuses on the Mirialan smuggler [Hylo Visz](/wiki/Hylo_Visz "Hylo Visz"), who is a major character in [the second entry](/wiki/Timeline_2:_The_Mandalorian_Blockade_is_Broken "Timeline 2: The Mandalorian Blockade is Broken") in the *Galactic Timeline* series. The story opens with Visz performing a job for [Barrga](/wiki/Barrga "Barrga") the Hutt, delivering a shipment to Corellia on her ship *[Crimson Fleece](/wiki/Crimson_Fleece "Crimson Fleece")*, but Visz is accompanied by Barrga's enforcers [Musk](/wiki/Musk_(Nikto) "Musk (Nikto)") and a [Weequay](/wiki/Unidentified_Weequay_enforcer "Unidentified Weequay enforcer"). The two enforcers stun Visz and cut her out of the deal with the [Rendili Vehicle Corporation](/wiki/Rendili_Vehicle_Corporation/Legends "Rendili Vehicle Corporation/Legends"), but Visz escapes from the *Fleece*'s cargo hold in time to witness the deal. The *Fleece* is destroyed by explosives after it takes off, as Rendili is double-crossing Barrga, and Visz searches the facility for a way to escape before discovering a prototype corvette. Visz steals the corvette from its Jedi pilot[[383]](#cite_note-Vanguard_Suv-383) and renames the vessel the [*Vanguard*](/wiki/Vanguard_(Defender-class_light_corvette) "Vanguard (Defender-class light corvette)"), which she later uses in the [breaking](/wiki/Battle_on_the_Hydian_Way "Battle on the Hydian Way") of the [Blockade of the Hydian Way](/wiki/Blockade_of_the_Hydian_Way "Blockade of the Hydian Way").[[23]](#cite_note-Encyclopedia-23) "Smuggler's Vanguard" introduces the *Defender*-class light corvette, the ship for both Jedi classes in *The Old Republic*, though the story initially described it as a *Vanguard*-class.[[383]](#cite_note-Vanguard_Suv-383) The *Encyclopedia* later resolved this contradiction by naming Visz's ship as the *Vanguard*.[[23]](#cite_note-Encyclopedia-23)

#### The Third Lesson

[![TheThirdLesson-SWI124](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/9/9d/TheThirdLesson-SWI124.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20111108032453)

:   [![icon](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/04/Blue_Glass_Arrow.svg/revision/latest?cb=20090726033133) Main article: [The Old Republic: The Third Lesson](/wiki/The_Old_Republic:_The_Third_Lesson "The Old Republic: The Third Lesson")

**"The Old Republic: The Third Lesson"** is a short story by Paul S. Kemp that was published on [March 2](/wiki/March_2 "March 2"), 2011 in [*Star Wars Insider* 124](/wiki/Star_Wars_Insider_124 "Star Wars Insider 124"). Set in the aftermath of the Battle of Alderaan, the events of which were depicted in the *Hope* trailer, the story reveals that Darth Malgus survived Satele Shan's attack and was evacuated from the battlefield. However, Malgus senses the presence of a Jedi in the ruins below him as his shuttle crosses Alderaan, and the Sith Lord forces the pilot to stop in order to defeat the Jedi. As he engages the [Zabrak Jedi](/wiki/Unidentified_Zabrak_Jedi_(Battle_of_Alderaan) "Unidentified Zabrak Jedi (Battle of Alderaan)") in battle, Malgus's thoughts return to his childhood as Veradun, when his [adoptive father](/wiki/Veradun%27s_adoptive_father "Veradun's adoptive father") showed the youth his private zoo. While fighting the Jedi, Malgus remembers three lessons that his father taught the young Veradun: savagery was only useful if controlled, trust no one, especially those who appeared to be weak, and that sometimes, there was only an empty cage. Back in the present, Malgus is able to defeat his opponent despite the presence of a second Jedi named [Vorin](/wiki/Vorin "Vorin"), as the Sith senses Vorin's presence and quickly kills him. The story closes with the death of the Zabrak Jedi, as Malgus continues to ponder his father's third lesson.[[385]](#cite_note-Third_Lesson-385)

#### The Last Battle of Colonel Jace Malcom

[![The Last Battle of Colonel Jace Malcom](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/5/5c/The_Last_Battle_of_Colonel_Jace_Malcom.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20121026175949)

:   [![icon](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/04/Blue_Glass_Arrow.svg/revision/latest?cb=20090726033133) Main article: [The Last Battle of Colonel Jace Malcom](/wiki/The_Last_Battle_of_Colonel_Jace_Malcom "The Last Battle of Colonel Jace Malcom")

***The Last Battle of Colonel Jace Malcom*** is a short story by Alexander Freed that appeared in [*Star Wars Insider* 137](/wiki/Star_Wars_Insider_137 "Star Wars Insider 137") in October 2012, and serves a lead-in to the novel *The Old Republic: Annihilation*. The story details Colonel Jace Malcom's assignment on the planet [Kalandis Seven](/wiki/Kalandis_Seven "Kalandis Seven"), where he is advising [Sergeant](/wiki/Sergeant/Legends "Sergeant/Legends") [Shanra Immel](/wiki/Shanra_Immel "Shanra Immel") and her [squad](/wiki/Shanra_Immel%27s_squad "Shanra Immel's squad") as they are tasked with placing homing beacons in the nearby Imperial-controlled [spaceport](/wiki/Kalandis_Seven%27s_spaceport "Kalandis Seven's spaceport") so that the Republic's starfighters can bomb it through the planet's fog. Immel's squad suffers casualties as they head toward their objective, and Malcom volunteers to infiltrate the Sith command ship as a distraction. His efforts result in the death of the [Sith commander](/wiki/Unidentified_Sith_Overseer "Unidentified Sith Overseer") and the destruction of the command ship, and he is saved from falling to his death by a [Jedi Knight's](/wiki/Unidentified_Jedi_Knight_(Kalandis_Seven) "Unidentified Jedi Knight (Kalandis Seven)") shuttle. The Knight informs Malcom that he is being recalled by Supreme Chancellor Saresh, and the Jedi takes the soldier back to Coruscant. Malcom is promoted to Supreme Commander by Saresh between the events of *The Last Battle* and *Annihilation*, and the story's events fall between the end of the Battle of Corellia and the beginning of *Rise of the Hutt Cartel*.[[386]](#cite_note-Last_Battle-386)

### Cinematic trailers

#### *Deceived*

[![MalgusLeaves-Deceived](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/9/99/MalgusLeaves-Deceived.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20110608003334)

:   [![icon](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/04/Blue_Glass_Arrow.svg/revision/latest?cb=20090726033133) Main article: [Deceived](/wiki/Deceived "Deceived")

:   "*Our time has come. For 300 years, we prepared. We grew stronger. While you rested in your cradle of power, believing your people were* safe*... and* protected*. You were trusted to* lead *the Republic—but you were deceived, as our powers of the dark side have blinded you. You assumed no force could challenge you...and now...*finally*...we have returned.*"
:   ―Darth Malgus during the invasion of the Jedi Temple — ![20?cb=20250116042720](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/e/ee/Quote-audio.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/20?cb=20250116042720) [Link](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/5/54/InvasionOfTheJediTemple.flac/revision/latest?cb=20250308175532)▶️ ([file info](/wiki/File:InvasionOfTheJediTemple.flac "File:InvasionOfTheJediTemple.flac"))[[9]](#cite_note-Manual-9)

The first cinematic trailer for *Star Wars: The Old Republic*, a 3:53 minute video entitled ***Deceived***, was released on June 1, 2009 at E3 2009. Developed by Blur Studios with the help of Skywalker Sound, *Deceived* is rendered in photo-realistic CGI and depicts Darth Malgus leading a Sith attack on the Jedi Temple during the Sacking of Coruscant. Malgus and his lover [Eleena Daru](/wiki/Eleena_Daru "Eleena Daru") enter the Temple shortly before a shuttle of Sith crashes into the structure, and in the resultant fight, the Mandalorian [Shae Vizla](/wiki/Mandalore_the_Avenger "Mandalore the Avenger") disables the planet's security grid while Malgus's Sith massacre the Jedi and Malgus himself kills Jedi Master [Ven Zallow](/wiki/Ven_Zallow "Ven Zallow") just before the Sacking begins. The trailer is narrated by Malgus, and it received praise from both fans[[141]](#cite_note-Deceived_page-141) and industry critics. An interview with Roger Evoy, LucasArts' marketing manager, led to confusion as to the game's chronological setting, as Evoy erroneously stated that the game was set between the original and prequel trilogies of movies. This also led some fans to criticize the trailer's technology, as it appeared rather similar to that of the prequel trilogy almost 4,000 years later. Fight choreography and motion capture for the trailer were externally utilized during the trailer's creation, while the soundtrack was mixed at Skywalker Sound, and BioWare and Industrial Light & Magic provided concept art and high-res models of the Jedi Temple and spacecraft so that Blur Studio could create a believable trailer.[[142]](#cite_note-Deceived_review-142) *Deceived* also received a follow-up novel, *The Old Republic: Deceived*, which expands on Malgus's role in the Sacking and the events that followed the attack.[[155]](#cite_note-Deceived-155)

#### *Hope*

[![HopeTrailer-TOR](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/5/5f/HopeTrailer-TOR.png/revision/latest?cb=20121119190532)

:   [![icon](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/04/Blue_Glass_Arrow.svg/revision/latest?cb=20090726033133) Main article: [Hope](/wiki/Hope_(cinematic_trailer) "Hope (cinematic trailer)")

:   "*For centuries, Alderaan stood as a beacon of hope in the Republic. But the Empire came, and with one savage strike, brought Alderaan to her knees. Now, time is running out as few are left to face the enemy. For those that remain, there is but one choice. We must fight—to victory, or death—for the Republic! […] While the sacrifices are heavy, we fight knowing that a single spark of courage can ignite the fires of hope, and restore peace across the galaxy.*"
:   ―Jace Malcom — ![20?cb=20250116042720](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/e/ee/Quote-audio.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/20?cb=20250116042720) [Link](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/1/17/HopeMonologue-TORHope.flac/revision/latest?cb=20250308175148)▶️ ([file info](/wiki/File:HopeMonologue-TORHope.flac "File:HopeMonologue-TORHope.flac"))[[150]](#cite_note-Hope-150)

The second cinematic trailer for *The Old Republic*, ***Hope***, was released on June 14, 2010, and the six-minute video was also developed by Blur Studio. *Hope* depicts the Battle of Alderaan, a major battle in the Great Galactic War, in which the Republic's elite Havoc Squad leads a suicidal charge against Darth Malgus and a significantly larger force. Havoc Squad, led by Captain [Jace Malcom](/wiki/Jace_Malcom "Jace Malcom"), has the element of surprise, but they soon begin to fall against the Sith and their more numerous Imperial soldiers. However, the arrival of the Jedi Knight Satele Shan sees Malcom rescued from execution and the two join forces to defeat Malgus, leaving the Sith buried beneath an entire mountain of rubble as the Republic forces claim victory.[[150]](#cite_note-Hope-150) *Hope*'s events were expanded on in the fourth *The Old Republic* novel, *Annihilation*, which explains that Shan had come to Malcom's rescue because of a Force vision and that the two began a secret affair in the aftermath of the battle that results in Shan's son Theron before the Jedi breaks it off.[[27]](#cite_note-Annihilation-27) Shan's appearance was radically different than how she appeared in the online comics, and this led to some confusion as to whether the game occurred ten or thirty years after the end of the Great Galactic War.[[18]](#cite_note-Time_Question-18)

#### *Return*

[![Malgus-Return](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/8/8e/Malgus-Return.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20220312174746)

:   [![icon](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/04/Blue_Glass_Arrow.svg/revision/latest?cb=20090726033133) Main article: [Return](/wiki/Return_(cinematic_trailer) "Return (cinematic trailer)")

:   "*Korriban, ancient birthplace of the Sith. We believed ruins were all that remained of their evil empire.*"
:   ―Satele Shan[[387]](#cite_note-Return_trailer-387)

***Return*** is the third cinematic trailer for *The Old Republic*, a 6:20 minute video that is set in the year 3681 BBY and depicts the Battle of Korriban, the beginning of the Great Galactic War. Released at E3 2011 on June 6, *Return* features appearances by a number of characters from the earlier trailers: Satele Shan and Jace Malcom from the *Hope* trailer, as well as Darth Malgus from both *Hope* and *Deceived* and the astromech droid T7-O1 who briefly appeared in *Deceived* and is a companion character for the Jedi Knight class. In *Return*, a Sith armada attacks the Republic space station above the Sith homeworld of Korriban in order to reclaim the planet, and Jedi Master [Kao Cen Darach](/wiki/Kao_Cen_Darach "Kao Cen Darach") attempts to escape the station and warn the Republic with his apprentice Satele Shan, the Republic trooper Jace Malcom, and the smuggler [Nico Okarr](/wiki/Nico_Okarr "Nico Okarr"), though Shan and Darach are forced to battle a young Malgus and his master [Vindican](/wiki/Darth_Vindican "Darth Vindican") to escape. In the fighting that follows, Shan, Malcom, and Okarr escape to the Republic, while Malgus slays his Master after killing Darach as the Sith fleet claims Korriban.[[157]](#cite_note-Return_News-157)

#### *HK-51 Revealed*

[![HK-51 Revealed](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/08/HK-51_Revealed.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20120717041450)

:   "*All these years lost, the most dangerous machines in the galaxy.*"
:   ―Narrator[[388]](#cite_note-HK-51_Revealed_announce-388)

***HK-51 Revealed*** is the fourth cinematic trailer for *The Old Republic*, a 1:53 minute video that was released on July 16, 2012. Unlike the other trailers, this does not depict a narrative, and instead is merely a teaser for the release of Game Update 1.5: HK-51 Activated and the addition of HK-51 as a companion character. It depicts a ship's insides as a narrator speaks, revealing scores of HK-51 assassin droids in storage. As one of the assassin droids activates the video comes to a close. The trailer was first shown to journalists at E3 2012, where a portion of the video was aired, and the trailer was officially premiered at San Diego Comic-Con and on the game's official website in July.[[388]](#cite_note-HK-51_Revealed_announce-388)

#### *Sacrifice*

[![SWTOR Sacrifice thumb](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/0e/SWTOR_Sacrifice_thumb.png/revision/latest?cb=20170925050731)

:   [![icon](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/04/Blue_Glass_Arrow.svg/revision/latest?cb=20090726033133) Main article: [Sacrifice](/wiki/Sacrifice_(cinematic_trailer) "Sacrifice (cinematic trailer)")

:   "*A man can have anything… if he is willing to sacrifice.*"
:   ―Valkorion[[389]](#cite_note-Sacrifice-389)

***Sacrifice*** is the fifth cinematic trailer for *The Old Republic*, a 4:23 minute video that introduces the storyline of the *Knights of the Fallen Empire* expansion. Released at E3 2015 on June 15, *Sacrifice* is narrated by Emperor Valkorion of the Eternal Empire and tells the story of his sons [Arcann](/wiki/Arcann "Arcann") and [Thexan](/wiki/Thexan "Thexan"). The two are trained from childhood to be warriors, and as adults, they lead their father's armies in overrunning the Republic and the Sith Empire. However, Arcann grows increasingly frustrated with Valkorion's apparent lack of interest or affection for his sons, and after he sustains serious injuries in battle—receiving heavy scarring and losing an arm that is replaced with a cybernetic one—he attacks his father when Valkorion seemingly ignores his sons' presentation of trophies from their conquests. Thexan pulls his brother back with the Force only moments before Arcann strikes Valkorion with his lightsaber, but in the brief duel that follows, Arcann kills his twin. As he comes to his senses while cradling Thexan, Valkorion approaches him and orders Arcann to come with him.[[390]](#cite_note-SacrificeTrailer-390)

#### *Betrayed*

[![VaylinDuel-Betrayed](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/f/f8/VaylinDuel-Betrayed.png/revision/latest?cb=20161129032805)

:   [![icon](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/04/Blue_Glass_Arrow.svg/revision/latest?cb=20090726033133) Main article: [Betrayed](/wiki/Betrayed "Betrayed")

***Betrayed*** is the sixth cinematic trailer for *The Old Republic*, a 6:09 minute video that was released on [October 7](/wiki/October_7 "October 7"), 2016 and introduces the storyline of the *Knights of the Eternal Throne* expansion. The trailer depicts the story of [Senya Tirall](/wiki/Senya_Tirall "Senya Tirall") and her daughter [Vaylin](/wiki/Vaylin "Vaylin"). Where Senya recalls moments from her daughter's childhood as she rescues her from the [Sanitarium](/wiki/Sanitarium "Sanitarium") on [Nathema](/wiki/Nathema "Nathema"), where Vaylin had been imprisoned by Valkorion to suppress her powers. Vaylin, who had trouble controlling her Force powers and was locked up by the [Nathema Zealots](/wiki/Nathema_Zealot "Nathema Zealot"), turns down Senya's offer to rescue her. Years later, Senya finds a ruined field on Ord Mantell, filled with dead Knights and Vaylin's old toy. As she prepares for a fight, a dark figure appears and sets the field on fire using the Force. Senya's lightsaber is pulled away, and she grabs a weapon from a fallen Knight just before Vaylin attacks her.[[391]](#cite_note-BetrayedTrailer-391)

#### *Disorder*

[![MalgusVsOrr-Disorder](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/e/e2/MalgusVsOrr-Disorder.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20220216154750)

:   [![icon](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/04/Blue_Glass_Arrow.svg/revision/latest?cb=20090726033133) Main article: [Disorder](/wiki/Disorder "Disorder")

***Disorder*** is the seventh cinematic trailer for *The Old Republic*, a 6:29 minute video that was released on [February 15](/wiki/February_15 "February 15"), 2022 alongside the [*Legacy of the Sith*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Old_Republic:_Legacy_of_the_Sith "Star Wars: The Old Republic: Legacy of the Sith") expansion. The trailer focuses on Jedi Master [Denolm Orr](/wiki/Denolm_Orr "Denolm Orr") and his Padawan, [Sa'har Kateen](/wiki/Sa%27har_Kateen "Sa'har Kateen") on a [mission](/wiki/Mission_to_Elom "Mission to Elom") to the [Temple of Nul](/wiki/Temple_of_Nul "Temple of Nul") on [Elom](/wiki/Elom_(planet)/Legends "Elom (planet)/Legends") to retrieve a special [holocron](/wiki/Darth_Nul%27s_holocron "Darth Nul's holocron") before the Sith Empire. While they were fighting a [Sith warrior](/wiki/Unidentified_Sith_warrior_(Elom) "Unidentified Sith warrior (Elom)"), the Sith was unexpectedly killed by a rogue Sith Lord Darth Malgus who had just entered the temple. While Malgus and Orr dueled, Sa'har entered a machine and saw a vision of her master abandoning her [brother](/wiki/Ri%27kan_Kateen "Ri'kan Kateen"). Orr destroyed the machine and tried to get the holocron from Sa'har, but their struggle allowed Malgus to defeat Orr and take the holocron for himself.[[347]](#cite_note-DisorderTrailer-347)

### *Galactic Timeline*

:   [![icon](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/04/Blue_Glass_Arrow.svg/revision/latest?cb=20090726033133) Main article: [Galactic Timeline](/wiki/Galactic_Timeline "Galactic Timeline")

The ***Galactic Timeline*** is a series of a dozen in-universe videos presented as historical records made for the [Jedi Archives](/wiki/Jedi_Archives/Legends "Jedi Archives/Legends") by Jedi Master Gnost-Dural. Beginning with the first entry on the Treaty of Coruscant, which was released on March 27, 2009, the videos described the history of the Republic, the Empire, the Jedi and Sith, and the recent Great Galactic War. The videos were released approximately every two months and continued in chronologically reverse order, with the first six entries dealing with the Great War and the following six gradually moving backwards in history. The Timeline was brought to an end following the release of Timeline 12: The Great Hyperspace War on February 11, 2011,[[140]](#cite_note-Galactic_Timeline-140) though a seven additional videos were originally planned that would have chronicled history as far back as the discovery of the Force on Tython. The series was discontinued on account of the developers' belief that the videos were becoming less relevant to the game.[[392]](#cite_note-RedditQA-392) The videos are still available on *The Old Republic*'s official site, which also presents the headings and dates for the seven unreleased videos.[[393]](#cite_note-History-393)

### Comic series

#### *Threat of Peace*

[![Threat of Peace](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/f/f3/Threat_of_Peace.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20090227182758)

:   [![icon](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/04/Blue_Glass_Arrow.svg/revision/latest?cb=20090726033133) Main article: [Star Wars: The Old Republic, Threat of Peace](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Old_Republic,_Threat_of_Peace "Star Wars: The Old Republic, Threat of Peace")

***Star Wars: The Old Republic, Threat of Peace*** was the first tie-in webcomic for the game, and was reprinted as the first arc in the *Star Wars: The Old Republic* comic series. Released on the game's official site, *Threat of Peace* was released in three issues over the course of 2009 and early 2010. Seven pages were released every other Friday on the game's official site for a total of 28 pages per issue. The three issues of the webcomic were later published as comic issue by Dark Horse in the months after the completion of the webcomic. *Threat of Peace* was written by [Robert Chestney](/wiki/Robert_Chestney "Robert Chestney") and pencilled by [Alex Sanchez](/wiki/Alex_Sanchez_(artist) "Alex Sanchez (artist)"), and was set in 3653 BBY, depicting the Treaty of Coruscant and its immediate aftermath. However, because the comic was developed and released several years before the release of *The Old Republic*, many visual elements of the game are drastically different from the final versions that appear in the game.[[394]](#cite_note-Threat_1-394)

In 3653 BBY, the Empire has requested a peace conference with the Republic on the planet Alderaan, and withdraw their forces from the [Minos Cluster](/wiki/Minos_Cluster/Legends "Minos Cluster/Legends") as a show of good faith. The Republic agrees sending a delegation including several Jedi and Senator [Paran Am-Ris](/wiki/Paran_Am-Ris "Paran Am-Ris") to meet with the Empire. Jedi Master Orgus Din and Lieutenant Harron Tavus return to Coruscant to report on the Empire's withdrawal, while Jedi Knight Satele Shan cannot quell her unease at Alderaan about the conference. Her suspicions are correct—as Din and Tavus leave the Senate Hall, the Empire launches an invasion of Coruscant, and when the Republic delegation witnesses the Sith Lord Darth Angral's murder of Supreme Chancellor [Berooken](/wiki/Berooken "Berooken") via holotransmission, the Sith envoys inform them that they are holding Coruscant hostage. The Republic is forced to sign the Treaty of Coruscant, and the Jedi are dispatched to battlefronts across the galaxy to enforce the withdrawal of Republic forces as stated in the agreement. Din is sent to Balmorra to deal with his former apprentice [Fortris Gall](/wiki/Fortris_Gall "Fortris Gall"), while Shan and her former Master [Dar'Nala](/wiki/Dar%27Nala "Dar'Nala") are sent on another assignment—but they are seemingly attacked by an Imperial vessel, and Shan is forced to flee in an escape pod.[[394]](#cite_note-Threat_1-394)

She is rescued by Din and Tavus, who take her with them to Balmorra, and Din forces Gall to stand down and accompany them on their next mission to [Dantooine](/wiki/Dantooine/Legends "Dantooine/Legends"). Meanwhile, Dar'Nala is apparently killed by the Sith after convincing the bounty hunter Braden to take word of the Sith's treachery to Coruscant. On Korriban, the Sith Lord Darth Baras is nearly killed in an attack he believes that his rival Angral is responsible for. On Coruscant, Braden tries to tell Grand Master [Zym](/wiki/Zym "Zym") of Dalborra's message, but Zym refuses to listen after Braden's murder of a [Republic captain](/wiki/Gin_Lesl "Gin Lesl"), and the bounty hunter kills Zym just before the Senate Tower is hit by a massive explosion.[[395]](#cite_note-Threat_2-395) The recent attacks have the Senate clamoring for a return to war, and when Gall, Din, Tavus, and Shan arrive on Dantooine, Gall convinces Tavus to meet him in a remote [cave system](/wiki/Crystal_Cave_(Dantooine) "Crystal Cave (Dantooine)"). There, the true culprit behind recent events is revealed—Dar'Nala is alive, and she has perpetrated the recent attacks in order to implicate the Empire and thus dissolve the Treaty. Shan pursues Tavus and discovers her Master, but when Angral and Baras—having discovered Dar'Nala's involvement in the attack on Baras—arrive at the cave, Shan realizes that Dar'Nala's hatred of the Sith has driven her to the dark side. Dar'Nala is killed by the Wookiee bounty hunter [Dalborra](/wiki/Dalborra "Dalborra"), and after a tense standoff, the Sith Lords depart and Gall, Shan, and Tavus decide to cover up Dar'Nala's involvement for the sake of the Treaty.[[396]](#cite_note-Threat_3-396)

*Threat of Peace* features a number of elements that visually differ from the finalized game.
